<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

		<!-- ngIf: !vm.loading --><div ng-if="!vm.loading" class="ng-scope">

	<div class="pure-g">
		<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage --><div ng-if="::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage" ng-class="vm.details.graphicalAbstract ? 'pure-u-14-24 u-pr-1' : 'pure-u-1-1'" class="ng-scope pure-u-1-1">
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement -->
		<!--/div-->
		<!--div ng-class="{'pure-u-14-24 u-pr-1':  vm.details.graphicalAbstract, 'pure-u-1-1': ! vm.details.graphicalAbstract}"-->
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract --><div ng-if="::vm.details.abstract" class="ng-scope">
				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">In this letter, a Yagi-Uda antenna with load and additional reflector is proposed to achieve strong and uniform magnetic field distribution within the antenna area for near-field ultrahigh-frequency radio frequency identification (RFID). This proposed antenna is composed of one driven dipole to emit electromagnetic (EM) wave, several directors to direct the EM wave to the desired area, a load element at the end of the director array to absorb the wave, and two reflectors at both ends to reflect the EM wave. The proposed antenna can generate a uniform magnetic field distribution within the antenna area, meanwhile keeping the field strength outside the antenna area relatively small. A prototype, as an example, that contains 13 elements is designed and fabricated, with the measured bandwidth of 880-980 MHz. The achieved interrogation area is 440 × 160 mm<sup>2</sup>, measured by utilizing a commercial RFID reader and some near-field tags. It is worth mentioning that the interrogation area can be extended by adding more directors to the antenna.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->			
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.scope -->
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.purpose -->
		</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage -->

	</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Recently, the near-field ultrahigh-frequency (UHF) radio frequency identification (RFID) system received much
 attention for working at short distance as reliably as low-frequency/high-frequency RFID 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, and it has found enormous
 application in item-level RFID, such as retail, healthcare, asset management, and so on 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3 4" id="context_ref_3 ref4_1">[3]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>.</p><p>Among the several strategies to realize near-field UHF RFID, the near-field magnetic (inductive) coupling technique
 received significant attention because of its stable performance in the near-field region 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. Generally, the near-field tags are placed parallel to the reader antenna,
 as illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. To identify the tags, the magnitude of the magnetic
 field normal to the surface of the tag (referred as |H<sub>z</sub>| herein after) should be greater than
 the threshold value <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 1.745em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-3"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.9em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-4" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-5"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-6"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-7"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-8"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-9" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-10" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">h</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">H_{\rm{th}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In this
 letter, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-11" role="math" style="width: 1.745em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-12"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-13"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.9em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-14" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">H<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-15"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-16"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-17"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-18"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-19" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-20" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">h</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">H_{\rm{th}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is about –30 
 dBA/m based on the performances of the tags and the reader employed <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>, 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>. In many applications, the reader antenna should generate a strong and
 uniform distributed magnetic field to ensure the reading rate in a large interrogation area. Besides, to avoid wrong
 identification (i.e., tags beyond this interrogation area can also be identified), the magnetic field outside this
 area should be small enough. Several efforts have been made to achieve a strong and uniform <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-21" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-22"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-23"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-24"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-25"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-26"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-27" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-28"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-29" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">H</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-30"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-31"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-32" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-33"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-34"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-35"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-36"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-37" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">\rm{ | }H_{z}\rm{| }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> distribution 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>, 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8 9 10" id="context_ref_8 ref9 ref10_1">[8]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a> over a large
 area. For example, a zero-phase-shift line loop antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a> was proposed to
 keep the current phase along the loop constant to achieve a uniform <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-38" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-39"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-40"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-41"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-42"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-43"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-44" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-45"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-46" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">H</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-47"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-48"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-49" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-50"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-51"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-52"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-53"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-54" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">\rm{|
 }H_{z}\rm{| }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> distribution in a large area. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>
, a coplanar stripline with large gap was used to generate a uniform <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-55" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-56"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-57"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-58"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-59"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-60"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-61" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-62"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-63" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">H</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-64"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-65"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-66" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-67"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-68"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-69"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-70"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-71" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">\rm{|
 }H_{z}\rm{| }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> distribution over a long but narrow area. Additionally, the antennas based
 on oppositely directed currents were also studied intensively in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9 10" id="context_ref_9 ref10_1">[9]</a>
–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a> to achieve strong <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX">
<span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-72" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-73"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-74"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-75"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-76"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-77"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-78" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-79"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-80" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">H</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-81"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-82"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-83" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-84"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-85"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-86"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-87"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-88" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">\rm{| }H_{z}\rm{| }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> over a big area.</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang1-2601115-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang1-2601115-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Diagram of near-field UHF RFID.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7546938/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p>In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>, the traveling wave emitted by an endfire antenna is employed by
 the authors, for the first time, to achieve uniform <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-89" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-90"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-91"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-92"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-93"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-94"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-95" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-96"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-97" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">H</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-98"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-99"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-100" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-101"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-102"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-103"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-104"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-105" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-7">\rm{| }H_{z}\rm{| }</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> distribution in the main lobe direction. However, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-106" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-107"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-108"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-109"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-110"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-111"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-112" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-113"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-114" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">H</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-115"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-116"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-117" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-118"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-119"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-120"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-121"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-122" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-8">\rm{| }H_{z}\rm{| }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> will decrease as the distance increases,
 and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-123" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-124"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-125"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-126"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-127"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-128"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-129" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-130"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-131" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">H</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-132"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-133"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-134" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-135"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-136"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-137"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-138"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-139" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-9">\rm{| }H_{z}\rm{| }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> outside the
 interrogation area is still very strong. As one of the most widely used endfire antennas, the Yagi–Uda antenna
 has been well studied for far-field applications <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a>. However, little study
 has been done on its near-field characteristics for near-field RFID. The electromagnetic (EM) wave of the
 Yagi–Uda antenna is traveling along the directors, and the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-10-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-140" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-141"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-142"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-143"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-144"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-145"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-146" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-147"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-148" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">H</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-149"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-150"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-151" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-152"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-153"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-154"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-155"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-156" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-10">\rm{|
 }H_{z}\rm{| }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> distribution in the near field is quite uniform over the antenna. Yet,
 unfortunately, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-157" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-158"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-159"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-160"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-161"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-162"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-163" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-164"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-165" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">H</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-166"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-167"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-168" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-169"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-170"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-171"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-172"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-173" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-11">\rm{| }H_{z}\rm{| }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> outside
 the antenna area is still very strong and should be decreased to a small value for near-field RFID applications.</p><p>In this letter, a new Yagi–Uda antenna with load and additional reflector is proposed to achieve strong and
 uniform <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-174" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-175"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-176"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-177"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-178"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-179"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-180" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-181"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-182" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">H</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-183"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-184"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-185" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-186"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-187"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-188"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-189"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-190" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-12">\rm{| }H_{z}\rm{| }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> distribution
 within the antenna area for near-field UHF RFID. As an example, a prototype that contains 13 elements is designed and
 fabricated. The measured bandwidth is 880–980 MHz. The achieved interrogation area is 440 ×
 160 mm<sup>2</sup>, which has been measured by utilizing a commercial RFID reader and some near-field tags. It is
 worth mentioning that the interrogation area can be extended by simply adding more directors to the antenna.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Antenna Configuration and Design</h2></div><p>The configuration of the proposed antenna is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>, which is
 composed of, from left to right, one source reflector, one driven element, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX">
<span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-191" role="math" style="width: 0.964em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.84em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-192"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-193"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-194"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-195" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-13">{N}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> directors, one load element, and one load reflector. As it is in fact a
 Yagi–Uda antenna, the driven element is a half-wavelength dipole that is connected to the source via a
 quarter-wavelength impedance-matching transmission line. The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-14-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-196" role="math" style="width: 0.964em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.84em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-197"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-198"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-199"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-200" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-14">{N}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> directors are employed to guide the EM wave to the desired area (that is, the area from
 the first director to the last director). The load element is used to absorb the EM wave at the end of directors. The
 two reflectors (i.e., the source reflector and the load reflector) are employed to confine the EM field in the antenna
 area and suppress the EM field outside the antenna area. Generally, the directors are slightly shorter than the driven
 element, whereas the reflectors are slightly longer than the driven element <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_2">[13]
</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_2">[14]</a>. Final design parameters are: <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-15-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-201" role="math" style="width: 3.066em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.766em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.71em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-202"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-203"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-204"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-205" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-206" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-207" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">9</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-15">{N = 9}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX">
<span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-16-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-208" role="math" style="width: 5.288em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-214"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-215"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-216"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-217"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-218" style="font-size: 70.7%; <span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-17-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-226" role="math" style="width: 6.489em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; </p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang2abc-2601115-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang2abc-2601115-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>Geometry and dimensions of (a) top, (b) bottom metal layer, and (c) the side view (only one element is
 plotted for simplicity) of the proposed antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7546938/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a> gives the simulated current distribution of the proposed antenna by
 ANSYS HFSS <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_2">[15]</a>. As can be seen from <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3
</a>, the magnitude and direction of the current on the directors vary along the forward direction, from the
 negative maxima to the positive maxima. By using the “animated plot” function of the software, one can
 observe the dynamic current distribution, and it is found that the location of the maximum current moves along the
 directors from the driven element to the load element, thus generating a traveling wave that can be used to produce a
 uniform magnetic field distribution.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang3-2601115-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang3-2601115-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>Simulated current distribution of the antenna, normalized to maximum surface current density of 17.8
 A/m, where frequency is 920 MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7546938/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The instantaneous <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-496" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; The same results can be
 obtained when time goes from (1/6)T to (2/6)T. As time goes on, every point within the antenna area will
 experience peak and valley.  distribution of the proposed antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7546938/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a> shows the simulated magnetic field distribution of the proposed
 antenna at observing height of 10, 50, and 100 mm, respectively. When the observing height is 10 and 50 mm,
 a strong magnetic field distribution with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-560" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; –30 dBA/m is achieved within the antenna area (–65 mm &lt; <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-577" role="math" style="width: 0.544em;  However, when the observing height is bigger than 100 mm, the uniformity of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-580" role="math" style="width: 1.865em;  decreases, and the magnetic field beyond the antenna area (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-597" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">y</script></tex-math></inline-formula>
 &gt; 365 mm) also increases when compared to that of 50-mm observing height. This is partially caused by the
 limitation of the load element and the load reflector. The load element and the load reflector are added to the end of
 the directors to absorb and reflect the EM field, so that the EM field beyond the antenna can be reduced. However,
 since the two newly added elements are located in the <i>xoy</i>-plane, their effects of absorbing and
 blocking the EM field will degrade as the observing height increases, which will lead to the increase of 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-603" role="math" style="width: 1.865em;  when the observing height is 100 mm.

 distribution of the antenna at different frequencies.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7546938/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-688" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-689"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-690"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-691"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-692"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-693"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-694" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-695"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-696" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">H</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-697"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-698"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-699" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-700"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-701"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-702"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-703"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-704" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">\rm{| }H_{z}\rm{| }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> distributions of
 the antenna with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-705" role="math" style="width: 0.964em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.84em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-706"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-707" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-49">N</script></tex-math></inline-formula> = 9, 18, and 27 are
 given in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>, while keeping <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX">
<span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-50-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-708" role="math" style="width: 1.084em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.96em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-709"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-710"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-711" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-712"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-713"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-714"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-715"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-716" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-50">d_{\rm{2}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as constant 30 mm. The corresponding total length of the antenna is 430,
 700, and 970 mm, respectively. The results of the three cases in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>
 are obtained with the same input power (17 dBm) of the antenna. The magnetic field within the antenna area remains a
 strong strength (|H<sub>z</sub>| &gt; –30 dBA/m) and uniform distribution even if the antenna
 is longer than 900 mm, although experiencing a slight decline in the field strength due to losses in the
 directors and little power leakage along the director array. The results in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7
</a> confirm that the interrogation area of the antenna can be enlarged by simply increasing the number of directors.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang7-2601115-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang7-2601115-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Simulated <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-717" role="math" style="width: 2.12em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.657em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1001.52em 2.715em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-718"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-719"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-720"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-721"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-722"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-723" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-724"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.128em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.112em 1000.73em 4.17em -999.997em); top: -3.965em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-725" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">H</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.833em; left: 0.731em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-726"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-727"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-728" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-729"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-730"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-731"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-732"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-733" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.413em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.421em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">\rm{| }H_{z}\rm{| }</script></tex-math></inline-formula>
 distribution of the antenna with different <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-734" role="math" style="width: 1.128em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.863em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1000.86em 2.384em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-735"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-736" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.069em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-52">N</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.
</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7546938/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Experiment Results and Discussion</h2></div><p>As shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>, a prototype of the proposed antenna has been fabricated
 with the standard printed circuit board process. The reflection coefficient of the antenna is measured by a network
 analyzer (Agilent 8722ES), as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a> together with the simulated
 results. The antenna exhibits a broadband property, which is from 880 to 980 MHz (with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-53-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-737" role="math" style="width: 2.165em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.925em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.8em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-738"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-739"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-740"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-741" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-742"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-743" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-744"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-745"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-746" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">11</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-747"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-748"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-749" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-53">| S_{11} |</script></tex-math></inline-formula> &lt; –10 dB).
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang8-2601115-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang8-2601115-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Photograph of the fabricated antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7546938/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang9-2601115-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang9-2601115-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>Simulated and measured reflection coefficient of the antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7546938/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The reading performance of the antenna is verified by a commercial RFID reader (Marktrace RFID UHF four-channel
 fixed reader MR6134E <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_3">[7]</a>) and near-field tags (Impinj J41, which meets
 standard EPC Class1 Gen2 <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_3">[6]</a>). <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a>
 displays the test setup, the same with <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_3">[10]</a>. The tags are coded according to
 their positions so that the interrogation area is plotted according to the reading result of each tag. The output
 power of the reader is set as 17 dBm, which is much smaller than the maximum available output power of the reader (30
 dBm).
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang10-2601115-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang10-2601115-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 10. </b><fig><p>Near-field RFID measurement experiment setup.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7546938/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11</a> shows the measured interrogation area of the prototype at the
 observing heights of 10, 50, and 100 mm. The test results show good agreement with the simulated <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-750" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-751"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-752"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-753"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-754"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-755"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-756" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-757"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-758" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">H</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-759"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-760"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-761" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-762"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-763"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-764"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-765"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-766" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-54">\rm{| }H_{z}\rm{| }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> distribution in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>. As can be seen, when the observing height is 10 mm, most of the
 tags (reading rate &gt; 95%) within the antenna area are successfully read, while the tag reading rate beyond
 the antenna area is relatively low. As the observing height increases, the interrogation area decreases. This is
 caused by the decrease of the field strength as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>. The measured
 maximum readable distance of the antenna, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12</a>, is about
 140 mm with the specified reader and tags.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang11abc-2601115-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang11abc-2601115-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 11. </b><fig><p>Measured readable area of the prototype at (a) 10, (b) 50, and (c) 100 mm.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7546938/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig12"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang12-2601115-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7546938/tang12-2601115-small.gif" alt="Figure 12" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 12. </b><fig><p>Measured maximum readable distance of the prototype.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7546938/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>In this letter, we propose a quasi-Yagi antenna to achieve a strong and uniform <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-767" role="math" style="width: 1.865em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.685em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-768"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-769"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-770"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-771"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-772"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-773" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-774"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-775" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">H</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-776"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-777"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-778" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-779"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-780"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-781"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-782"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-783" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">\rm{| }H_{z}\rm{| }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> distribution within the antenna area for
 near-field UHF RFID application. The magnetic field outside the antenna area is eliminated by a load element and two
 reflectors. A prototype that contains 13 elements in total has been designed and fabricated. The magnetic field
 distribution of the antenna is verified by a commercial RFID reader and some near-field tags, and a large
 interrogation area of 440 × 160 mm<sup>2</sup> is realized, which is exactly the area of the antenna. It is
 worth mentioning that the interrogation area of the proposed antenna can be extended by adding more directors to the
 antenna.</p></div>
</div></div>

	<h2 class="document-ft-section-header">Keywords</h2>
	
	<!-- ngIf: !vm.contextData.keywords.length -->

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		}
	}
});

</script>

RFID","abstract":"In this letter, a Yagi-Uda antenna with load and additional reflector is proposed to achieve strong and uniform magnetic field distribution within the antenna area for near-field ultrahigh-frequency radio frequency identification (RFID). This proposed antenna is composed of one driven dipole to emit electromagnetic (EM) wave, several directors to direct the EM wave to the desired area, a load element at the end of the director array to absorb the wave, and two reflectors at both ends to reflect the EM wave. The proposed antenna can generate a uniform magnetic field distribution within the antenna area, meanwhile keeping the field strength outside the antenna area relatively small. A prototype, as an example, that contains 13 elements is designed and fabricated, with the measured bandwidth of 880-980 MHz. The achieved interrogation area is 440 &amp;#x00D7; 160 mm&lt;sup&gt;2&lt;/sup&gt;, measured by utilizing a commercial RFID reader and some near-field tags.
